The ascii output from the pdf before filtering etc.

Proceedings of the New York state conventions for "rescuing the

canals from the ruin with which they are threatened": --by exposing

and resisting "the railroad conspiracy" for "discrediting the canals,

and diminishing their revenues, with a view of bringing them under

the hammer":--and adopting measures for counteracting "the ruinous

competition with railroads, permitted by the state, and instituted

by railroad directors for the express purpose of breaking down the

credit of the canals."--... With replies from nominees, of all parties,

for state offices, opinions of the New York Chamber of commerce,

and statistics and explanations concerning the canal system and

the railway operations, in connection with the public rights and

revenues, and the agricultural, manufacturing & commercial interests

of the state ...

Clinton league for promoting the completion of the canal system.

New York, Printed for the Clinton league, by Baker & Godwin, 1859.

* "A Convention of Citizens of the State of New York, * * * held at Rochester, * * * to devise measures

to RESCUE THE CANALS FROM THE RUIN WITH WHICH THEY ARE THREATENED," says the

Editor of the New York Herald, August 31, 1859.

t "The Railroad Interest has blundered a premature charge upon the Canals," says the New York Daily Times,

edited by Ex-Lieutenant Governor Raymond. * * * "Fortunate, then, for the State, was this premature

publication of the Railroad Conspiracy," continues the Daily Times of Sept. 3d. " The announcement rallied

the Friends of the Canals at an auspicious moment. Had the alarm been given a week later, the political

conventions might have ignored the whole question, and at least a year would have been lost. But, now,

this is impossible." * * * "How wisely the (Rochester) Convention has performed its delicate and important duties, may be seen by our report of its proceedings."-(N. Y. Times, Sept. 3, 1859.)

$ "It is proposed to sell the Canals," says the New York Tribune. "A sale, even of the Internal Improvements of

the State, is not necessarily objectionable; but it happens, in this case, unfortunately, that the proposition to

sell comes from those, or the friends of those, who wish to buty."-(N. Y. Tribune, Sept. 5.)

Generated on 2014-09-10 01:37 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/miun.ahj1423.0001.001

Public Domain / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd

"Even if we granted-which we do not for a moment-that the Canals are likely to prove a bad property," continues the New York Tribune, "we contend that the worst possible thing we could do with them would be to

part with them, when an absolute and demonstrable certainty exists that THEY WOULD BE USED AS A

MIGHTY INSTRUMENT FOR THE POLITICAL AND PECUNIARY OPPRESSION OF THE PEOPLE AT

LARGE."-(N. Y. Tribune, Sept. 5.)

"Do the Canals tas the Treasury? Persistent and apparently concerted efforts are now making all over the State,

to convince the People that the Canals are a dead-weight upon the Treasury, and that their retention by the

Commonwealth will involve the necessity of direct taxation for their support. 1

A more UNFOUNDED

ABSURDITY (says the New York Times) WAS NEVER PUT FORTH by a knot of FINANCIAL CONSPIRATORS bent upon HOODWINKING THE PUBLIC MIND." * * * * "The truth is (says the Editor

of the Times) that THE CANALS, instead of being burdensome and unproductive, are actually at this moment BETTER PROPERTY TIAN ANY RAILWAY IN THE STATE."-New York Times.

" The place which they (the Canals) fill in our system of internal communication is one which no railway can

supply, and in which they are not likely to meet the competition of new Canals. Nobody dreams of abolishing them. Were the State to be dragooned into selling them to-morrow, we should have the same men gambling in their stock, before a month was past, who now make the vast properties of the Railways the sport

of their speculations; and all that is required to make the public sentiment of the Commonwealth thoroughly

alive to their importance, is, to set the facts of their history clearly and honestly forth."-N. Y. Tribune.

" The prosperity of the State depends, to a certain degree, upon its traffic; its traffic must, in a large measure, be

carried on through ITS CANALS, which BELONG TO THE PEOPLE; the people, therefore, will directly,

as well as indirectly, enjoy the fruit of their own prosperity. Secondly: ALL MONOPOLIES ARE HOSTILE

TO THE INTERESTS OF THE PEOPLE. To throw into the same hands both the Railroads and the Canals

of the State, would be to give to private individuals the monopoly of all its internal transportation, and the

power greatly to oppress the people. It is wise and best, therefore, to avoid the creation of such a monopoly,

by keeping the Canals in the possession of the State, and under the control of the people themselves."New York Tribune.

NEW YORK:-PRINTED FOR THE CLINTON LEAGUE, BY BAKER &'GODWIN.'C'9Q ER, 1859,

REPORT TO THE CLINTON LEAGUE,

INCLUDING PROCEEDINGS OF

CONVENTIONS OF THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEW YORK

(AT ROCHESTER AND UTICA) CONCERNING THE

Canal System, Railway Management, and State Interests Generally.

IN addition to the " Brief Report," and other documents issued recently concerning the objects of the Rochester

STATE CONVENTION, and the motives of the New York Meetings in sending Delegates to that Convention, the undersigned, Chairman and Secretary (of those Meetings (known as the " CLINTON LEAGUE for Promoting the Completion of

the Canal System"), now respectfully present a FULL REPORT of the Proceedings of that Convention, and also of the

Utica Convention, printed from the statement of the phonographers employed for that purpose, in accordance with

the views of the meetings above mentioned.

This FULL REPORT embodies an amount of statistics and other facts, with expositions of Canal and Railway Operations, which make it well worthy of preservation for reference, in connection with present controversies, and with

the future policy of the State concerning the Commercial, Agricultural, and Manufacturing Interests of the whole

community.

As the Rochester Convention reiterated the doctrines of the Syracuse Convention on the same subjects, the

Address of the latter body is included as an Appendix in this pamphlet.

The Addresses of the Syracuse and Rochester Conventions-the first, written by Dr. S. B. HUNT, of Buffalo, and

the latter by ANSEL BAScoM, Esq., of Seneca Falls,-with the letters of Gov. HUNT, Gov. BOUCK, the Hon. SAMUEL

B. RUGGLES. and other matters, such as the speech of Gen. ADAMS, and the statements of Messrs. JAMES L. BARTON

GEO. R. BABCOCK, and CARLOS COBB, of Buffalo, should be widely circulated and carefully considered; as should,

also, the speeches of Ex-speaker ALVORD and Ex-speaker LITTLEJOHN, and of Mr. CROCKER, of Oswego, and Mr.

lHovEY. of Syracuse, in the Utica Convention, concerning the abuses of the Railway System, and the policy of the

Canal Enlargement, and concerning also particularly a Pro-Rata Law, for correcting the enormous evils resulting

from that pernicious discriminating Railway poiicy" whereby the people of this State are victimized in "the Railroad Conspiracy, (as the New York Times calls it), for discrediting the Canals and diminishing their Revenues, with

a view of bringing them under the hammer."

The Address from the undersigned, included in this pamphlet, briefly indicates the general views which prompted

the New York Meetings to send Delegates to the Rochester and Utica Conventions, and which now stimulate the

CLINTON LEAGUE to continued effort for " promoting the completion of the Canal System."

The foregoing matters have been printed in compact form, for general circulation-as presenting briefly the

essential points in discussion.

A few extracts from leading newspapers have been added-from the Herald, Tinzes, and Tribune-indicating

the effect produced by the movements connected with the objects for which the Rochester State Convention was

assembled. Attention is specially invited to these editorials. The necessity for that Convention, and its importance

in arousing ALL PARTIES, are briefly and forcibly exemplified in the editorial remarks quoted in this connection

from those influentialjournals. (Vide pages 3, 4, and 5.)

As one of the New York papers, however, stated that the recent movements concerning the Canal System are

uncalled-for assumptions of power by unauthorized persons, and as this statement has been copied by some other

Generated on 2014-09-10 01:37 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/miun.ahj1423.0001.001

Public Domain / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd

papers, it may be proper to state that the meetings in New York which appointed Delegates to the Rochester and Utica

Conventions, included men who wrote and sustained the first memorials anrd resolutions in the original movements (a

quarter-century ago) for Enlarging the Erie Canal-with men who have been life-long connected with the Commerce of

New York and the Western States men representing Transportation Companies which annually transact a larger

business between the Atlantic and the Interior States than all the "great Railroad Companies" of the United States

put together. (Vide Proceedings of Clinton League, page 5.)

It will be seen that the views of the CLINTON LEAGIUE-about questions to candidates-for a Pro-Rata Law, but

against reimposing Tolls on railroad freight,-and also against separate partisan organization or expression of preferces fr candidates-bave met with general approval. The proceedings of the State Executive Committee, the day

after the State Convention at Utica. are particularly worthy of notice on these points. (Vide pages 5 and 6 )

Inaccuracies of newspaper telegraph reports, published in the daily papers nearly everywhere in the State, will be

noticed on comparison of those telegrams with the Report published by the Editor of the Utica Morning Herald, as

well as with the Report of the phonographers published in this pamphlet. One only of these inaccurcacies will be

here mentioned, and this particularly concerns an important subject on which the New York delegates were specially

instructed, namely, against separate partisan organization up)on the Canal ques ion. The Associated Press reports in this City and throughout the State, (as far as we have seen), state that resolutions "providng." among other

things, "for committees to conduct the Legislative elections, were adopted." T his is utterly incorrect. No such

object was avowed, and no such committee was apppointed bv the Convention. On the contrary, the opinion of the

Convention, like the opinion previously expressed by the Clinton League in New Yrk, (as stated by the undersigned

in that Convention), was ilnanimously opposed to partisan organization-rtliance being placed on the' success of appeals to thec good sense of all parties, alter proper questions propounded to the candidates of all parties.

The Replies of Candidates are printed in the order of reception by us. All answered waho wuere questioned.

The replies were printed in the order of reception, and furnished in the same order t, editors and reporters who

desired copies. The last of these replies was not received till the 11th October; and this Report, including all the

correspondence with candidates for State Offices, is printed on the following (lay (12th October). ST All the

rieplies are favorable to the views exprvestsed ly tlhe Clinton Leyague, as presented in the questions, and approved

by the Execultive Conlmmittee of the State (onventions of the Friends of the Canal System. (Vide pages 5, 6, 7, &c.)

With this statement. it is scarcely necessary to add, that no delegate or member of this League had any concern in

telegraphing the reply of any one candidate (to the exclusion of others) to newspapers throughout the State.

The recent declarations of the several political State Conventions-the avowals of candidates nominated by all

parties for State Offices. in reply to tlie interr(ogatories propounded by this Association-indicate that the MORAL

INFLUENCE of the CLINTON LEAGUE can be exerted more pwertully in appealing to the GOOD SENSE OF ALI

PARTIES AN D ALL CANDII)ATES, than in separate partisan organization.

As several members of the Delegation appointed in New York were unable to attend the Conventions, it is

proper to add that "the names of the Delegates were all used authoritatively; and that, if not pre-ent in person, al

were there in spirit." as stated by one of the Delegates in the Convention. The extent to which that spirit was mani

fested may be inferred from the letter of the lion. SAMUEL B. RUGGLES. the chief of the Delegation, whose absence

VIEWS OF THE CLINTON LEAGUE,

EXPRESSED AT A MEETING PRIOR TO THE STATE CONVENTION AT UTICA: And as shown in the

QUESTIONS TO CANDIDATES of all parties, and in the movement for a Pro-Rata Bill, but AGAINST Tolling Railroads and AGAINST separate partisan organization.

AT a meeting of the "CLINTON LAGCUE," held at the Transportation Building, No. 100 Broad street, New

York, on the 24th September, 1859, copies of the various publications issued during the month were submitted for

Generated on 2014-09-10 01:37 GMT / http://hdl.handle.net/2027/miun.ahj1423.0001.001

Public Domain / http://www.hathitrust.org/access_use#pd

consideration, and approved.

After full considera'ion of the subjects involved in the documents, and especially of the subjects presented in

the QUESTIONS FOR CANDIDATES, which had been addressed to the NOMINEES OF ALL PARTIFS for State offices, and

after remarks from Messrs. Mallory, Caleb, Dane, Clark, White, Eats-n, James, Lowe, Hovey, Neal, Stark, Littlejohn,

Reynolds, Ladd, Rice, Allen, Kimball, Collier, and others-representing twenty of tile Transportation Companies

engaged in freighting between the Atlantic and Interior States-the suggestions touching the propliety of indtructing delegates to vote in the Utica Convention against re-imposing tolls on railroads, and also against separate

partisan organization or the expression of preferences among candidates, were unani2nously approved; and the following resolutions were adopted in accordance with the sentiments of the meeting:

Resolved, That the interrogatories propounded to the several nominees of all parties for State offices, by the

Chairman and Secretary of this Association, be accepted and approved, as embodying all the points which this

League considers essential for promoting the cause at the present time; that the said interrogatories, with all replies

that may be received, be reported to the State Executive Committee, and be published for the information of people

qf all parties, concerning the views ot the candidates of all parties touching the Canal and Railway questions now

before the people of the State of New York.

Resolved also, That, in the opinion of this Association, it is INEXPEDIENT TO REIMPOSE TOLLS UPON RAILROADS,

or to advocate such policy; though, as a matter of right and justice, it is highly equitable towards the tax-payers of the

State that the freight passing through the State over our Canals and Railways should contribute to paying off the

Public Debt, created for aiding those improvements.

Resolved, That the delegates named by this Association, who may attend the State Convention, at Utica, on the

2Sth Sept, be instructed to oppose all attempts to nominate State officers, or otherwise to engage this Association

in any partisan operations.

Resolved, That the next meeting of this League be held when the Chairman and Secretary can submit printed

copies of the proceedings of the Convention, and the answrers of the candidates of all parties, to the questions propounded on behalf of this Association.

HENRY O'RIELLY, Chairman.

HUG-H ALLEN, Secretary.
